## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and possibly explicit time t, which is the standard state-space form of (non)linear oscillator equations. Common physics structure is a restoring force depending on x (often from a potential), plus damping depending on v, plus optional external/parametric forcing depending on t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear spring (simple harmonic oscillator): dv_dt = -c0 * x (Hookean restoring force, no damping/forcing)
- Viscous damping oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (linear damping proportional to velocity)
- Time-varying damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - (c1 + c2 * cos(c3 * t)) * v (periodically modulated dissipation)
- Pure cubic stiffness: dv_dt = -c0 * x**3 (dominant nonlinear restoring force from quartic potential)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness + damping): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring with viscous loss)
- Higher-order polynomial potential gradient: dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) - c3 * v (anharmonic restoring force expansion)
- Quadratic position-dependent damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * (c2 + x**2) * v (damping increases with displacement amplitude)
- Nonlinear velocity drag (Rayleigh-type): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v**3 (stronger dissipation at high speed)
- Van der Pol oscillator (self-excited/limit cycle): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (negative damping at small |x|, positive at large |x|)
- Sinusoidally driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (external periodic forcing)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (nonlinear resonance and bistability)
- Parametric stiffness modulation (Mathieu-type): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (parametric excitation through time-varying stiffness)
- Dry-friction-like damping (smooth Coulomb friction): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * tanh(c3 * v) (approximates constant-magnitude friction with smooth sign transition)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring-force symmetry: conservative oscillators typically have dv_dt as an odd function of x (e.g., -c0*x - c1*x**3), reflecting symmetric potentials U(x).
- Potential-energy interpretation: if damping/forcing are absent, dv_dt often matches -dU/dx, so polynomial-in-x structures suggest an underlying polynomial potential.
- Amplitude-dependent frequency: adding x**3 (Duffing) produces frequency shifts with amplitude; look for dv_dt containing both x and x**3 when data show non-isochronous oscillations.
- Energy dissipation signature: terms proportional to -v (or -v**3) imply monotone mechanical energy loss per cycle; stronger-than-linear drag indicates faster decay at large |v|.
- Limit-cycle self-oscillation: a factor like (c0 - x**2) * v indicates negative damping near the origin and positive damping at large amplitude, leading to a stable oscillation amplitude.
- External periodic forcing: presence of sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms implies phase-locked steady responses, resonance peaks, and possible subharmonics in dv_dt.
- Parametric resonance indicator: a product cos(c*t) * x (time-periodic stiffness) can create instability bands; look for explicit t multiplying x rather than adding as a separate forcing term.
- Dry friction / stick-slip tendency: tanh(c*v) (or sign(v)) components cause near-constant deceleration opposing motion and can flatten velocity near turning points.
- Autonomous vs non-autonomous distinction: if dv_dt depends only on x and v (no explicit t), trajectories are time-translation invariant; explicit t terms indicate driven/parametric systems.

Key required structures:
- \(x^3\) term only (no other \(x\)-dependence), coefficient \(-2.9429...\)
- exactly one sinusoid in \(t\): \(0.5691...\sin(t)\) (cos allowed via phase shift)

- no constants, no linear \(v\), no other nonlinearities.

Below, for each candidate, I check whether we can set its free constants to reproduce exactly those four terms and kill everything else. Trig note: \(A\sin(\omega t+\phi)+B\cos(\omega t+\psi)\) can be reduced to a single sinusoid at the same frequency; but GT has frequency 1 and no extra frequencies.

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.0907*v**3 - 0.5945*v*exp(-Abs(v)) - 2.9429*x**3 + 0.5691*sin(t)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `x**3`
2. `sin(t)` (with frequency 1, no phase shift needed beyond what c allows)
3. `v**3`
4. `v*exp(-Abs(v))`

Key observation: `v**3 = v*Abs(v)**2` when v can be positive or negative. This is because `v * |v|^2 = v * v^2 = v^3`. So `v**3` and `v*Abs(v)**2` are equivalent.

Also, the GT has `exp(-Abs(v))` in the term `v*exp(-Abs(v))`, so candidates need `c*Abs(v)` in the exponent with c being freely set to -1.

Let me now check each candidate systematically. A candidate matches if, by choosing appropriate constants, all extra terms can be zeroed out and the remaining terms match the GT's basis functions.

For each candidate, I need:
- `x**3` term ✓
- `sin(t)` term (with c2=1, c3=0 or equivalent phase) ✓
- `v**3` OR `v*Abs(v)**2` term ✓
- `v*exp(c*Abs(v))` term ✓
- All other terms must be eliminable (set coefficients to 0)
